of this is feeling really tired or weak."

- Texto: "Premenopausal Stage
For women with regular periods, estradiol levels naturally rise and fall during follicular phase, ovulation, and luteal phase.
These fluctuations are completely normal, however if levels are too high or too low, it could indicate hormone-related concerns like polycystic ovary syndrome (PCOS) or low ovarian reserve.
Perimenopausal Stage
Hormone levels are typically all over the place. Estrogen levels could instantly drop during this phase which leads to symptoms like hot flashes, mood swings, or irregular periods.
Postmenopausal Stage
You’re considered postmenopausal if you’ve gone a full year without a period. Estradiol levels are expected to drop but critically low levels increases risk of bone thinning, heart disease, and vaginal dryness."

- Texto: "NUTRIENTS THAT COMPETE FOR ABSORPTION

Calcium + Magnesium

Often bundled together for bone and muscle health, high doses can cause them to compete in your gut – reducing absorption and counteracting their benefits.

Tip: Split the doses – Take your calcium in the morning and a magnesium supplement at night for sleep and muscle relaxation.

Iron + Zinc

Both are essential minerals, but they share the same absorption pathway. High doses of one can block the other, limiting their benefits.

Tip: Take zinc in the morning and iron later in the day, or use a balanced supplement with the right ratio."

- Texto: "NUTRIENTS THAT NEED TO STAY IN BALANCE

Vitamin D + K

Vitamin D helps your body absorb calcium, while vitamin K2 directs it into your bones and teeth instead of your arteries. Without enough K2, high vitamin D intake – especially with calcium – can contribute to calcium buildup in blood vessels.

Tip: Pair vitamin D3 with K2 for better bone health and to help prevent arterial calcification. Fermented foods like natto and hard cheeses are also natural K2 sources.

Zinc + Copper

Zinc supports immunity and healing, while copper helps make red blood cells and protect against oxidative stress. But they share the same transporter in the gut – too much zinc can block copper absorption, leading to deficiency over time.

Tip: If you take zinc regularly, be sure to get copper too – ideally in a 10:1 or 15:1 zinc-to-copper ratio."

Vitamin C + B12

Vitamin C boosts immunity, while B12 supports nerve health and red blood cell production. But high doses of vitamin C can break down B12, making it harder to absorb.

Tip: Take B12 in the morning and vitamin C later in the day, spacing them at least two hours apart.

Vitamin A + E

Vitamin A is best for good vision, healthy skin, and a strong immune system, while vitamin E protects your cells from oxidative stress. Over supplementing on Vitamin E messes with Vitamin A absorption.

Tip: Stick to moderate doses unless advised by a healthcare professional, and avoid pairing high-dose E with A unless in a balanced formula."

Optimal: < 5.2%
A long-term blood sugar marker that reflects your 3-month average glucose levels. When elevated, it's strongly linked to higher risk of mortality, cardiovascular disease, cancer, and dementia.
You can lower it through caloric restriction, regular exercise, and a low-carb, high-fat diet—plus support from supplements like ALA, magnesium, and berberine, or medications such as GLP-1s, Metformin, and SGLT2 inhibitors."
- Paleta: #44403D · #FFFFFF
- Prompt:

- Texto: "5 HDL-C – the cleaner
Optimal > 60 mg/dL

To raise it, incorporate HIIT and strength training, reduce sugar, and eat more monounsaturated fats, omega-3s, and polyphenol-rich foods like dark chocolate and berries. Supplements such as omega-3s, curcumin, and astaxanthin can help, along with prescriptions like fibrates, statins, and PCSK9 inhibitors."
